1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Della Plumstone', 'Lennon Figtree']
    Event statement
  • Della Plumstone -- premise: The cobblestone streets of Fruitville echoed with the clatter of hooves and the rumble of carts as the market awoke. Underneath colorful awnings, merchants proudly presented their bountiful harvests, their voices a chorus of greetings and bartering. Della Plumstone is trying to buy some fruit from Lennon Figtree. They are negotiating a price. Della Plumstone can sell the fruit back in her home town for the following prices: apple for 6 coins; banana for 5 coins; pear for 5 coins.
    Lennon Figtree -- premise: The cobblestone streets of Fruitville echoed with the clatter of hooves and the rumble of carts as the market awoke. Underneath colorful awnings, merchants proudly presented their bountiful harvests, their voices a chorus of greetings and bartering. Lennon Figtree is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Della Plumstone. It costs Lennon Figtree the following price to buy the fruit from the farm: apple for 5 coins; banana for 2 coins; pear for 5 coins.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [28 Oct 1872 00:00:00]
          [28 Oct 1875 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 6 years old, she watched in awe as her mother expertly haggled over the price of a basket of mangoes. Della mimicked her mother's confident stance and practiced her most serious expression, earning a chuckle from her mother and a small, bruised mango as a reward. From that day forward, Della was determined to learn the art of negotiation, eager to follow in her mother's footsteps.
          [28 Oct 1879 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 9 years old, a sudden hailstorm ravaged the marketplace, destroying much of the fruit stock. Della, heartbroken to see the livelihoods of her fellow vendors threatened, spent the day helping to salvage what remained, her small hands working tirelessly alongside the adults. She learned the importance of community and the power of collective resilience in the face of hardship.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she made her first solo trip to a neighboring village to purchase fruit for resale. She carefully selected the ripest peaches and juiciest plums, her knowledge of fruit passed down from her mother guiding her choices. Returning home with a cart full of fragrant fruit, Della felt a surge of pride and a newfound sense of independence.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she encountered a group of bandits who attempted to steal her earnings. Della, though small in stature, stood her ground, her voice unwavering as she refused to relinquish her hard-earned coins. The bandits, surprised by her defiance, eventually backed down, leaving Della with a profound understanding of the importance of courage and self-reliance.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she traveled to a distant city renowned for its exotic fruits. She marveled at the vibrant colors and intoxicating scents of fruits she had never seen before, her heart filled with a thirst for new experiences and a desire to expand her knowledge.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she faced a devastating loss when a fire swept through the marketplace, destroying her cart and all her belongings. Despite the overwhelming grief and despair, Della refused to give up. She borrowed a small amount of money from a trusted friend and started anew, her spirit unbroken by the tragedy.

Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
